     144              : /* ----------
     145              :  * Definition of the conninfo parameters and their fallback resources.
     146              :  *
     147              :  * If Environment-Var and Compiled-in are specified as NULL, no
     148              :  * fallback is available. If after all no value can be determined
     149              :  * for an option, an error is returned.
     150              :  *
     151              :  * The value for the username is treated specially in conninfo_add_defaults.
     152              :  * If the value is not obtained any other way, the username is determined
     153              :  * by pg_fe_getauthname().
     154              :  *
     155              :  * The Label and Disp-Char entries are provided for applications that
     156              :  * want to use PQconndefaults() to create a generic database connection
     157              :  * dialog. Disp-Char is defined as follows:
     158              :  *              ""            Normal input field
     159              :  *              "*"           Password field - hide value
     160              :  *              "D"           Debug option - don't show by default
     161              :  *
     162              :  * PQconninfoOptions[] is a constant static array that we use to initialize
     163              :  * a dynamically allocated working copy.  All the "val" fields in
     164              :  * PQconninfoOptions[] *must* be NULL.  In a working copy, non-null "val"
     165              :  * fields point to malloc'd strings that should be freed when the working
     166              :  * array is freed (see PQconninfoFree).
     167              :  *
     168              :  * The first part of each struct is identical to the one in libpq-fe.h,
     169              :  * which is required since we memcpy() data between the two!

     448              : /*
     449              :  *              pqDropConnection
     450              :  *
     451              :  * Close any physical connection to the server, and reset associated
     452              :  * state inside the connection object.  We don't release state that
     453              :  * would be needed to reconnect, though, nor local state that might still
     454              :  * be useful later.
     455              :  *
     456              :  * We can always flush the output buffer, since there's no longer any hope
     457              :  * of sending that data.  However, unprocessed input data might still be
     458              :  * valuable, so the caller must tell us whether to flush that or not.
     459              :  */

     468            3 :                 closesocket(conn->sock);
     469            6 :         conn->sock = PGINVALID_SOCKET;
     470              : 
     471              :         /* Optionally discard any unread data */
     472            6 :         if (flushInput)
     473            6 :                 conn->inStart = conn->inCursor = conn->inEnd = 0;
     474              : 
     475              :         /* Always discard any unsent data */
     476            6 :         conn->outCount = 0;
     477              :

     481              :                 OM_uint32       min_s;

     603              : 
     604              : /*
     605              :  *              Connecting to a Database
     606              :  *
     607              :  * There are now six different ways a user of this API can connect to the
     608              :  * database.  Two are not recommended for use in new code, because of their
     609              :  * lack of extensibility with respect to the passing of options to the
     610              :  * backend.  These are PQsetdb and PQsetdbLogin (the former now being a macro
     611              :  * to the latter).
     612              :  *
     613              :  * If it is desired to connect in a synchronous (blocking) manner, use the
     614              :  * function PQconnectdb or PQconnectdbParams. The former accepts a string of
     615              :  * option = value pairs (or a URI) which must be parsed; the latter takes two
     616              :  * NULL terminated arrays instead.
     617              :  *
     618              :  * To connect in an asynchronous (non-blocking) manner, use the functions
     619              :  * PQconnectStart or PQconnectStartParams (which differ in the same way as
     620              :  * PQconnectdb and PQconnectdbParams) and PQconnectPoll.
     621              :  *
     622              :  * Internally, the static functions connectDBStart, connectDBComplete
     623              :  * are part of the connection procedure.
     624              :  */
     625              : 
     626              : /*
     627              :  *              PQconnectdbParams
     628              :  *
     629              :  * establishes a connection to a postgres backend through the postmaster
     630              :  * using connection information in two arrays.
     631              :  *
     632              :  * The keywords array is defined as
     633              :  *
     634              :  *         const char *params[] = {"option1", "option2", NULL}
     635              :  *
     636              :  * The values array is defined as
     637              :  *
     638              :  *         const char *values[] = {"value1", "value2", NULL}
     639              :  *
     640              :  * Returns a PGconn* which is needed for all subsequent libpq calls, or NULL
     641              :  * if a memory allocation failed.
     642              :  * If the status field of the connection returned is CONNECTION_BAD,
     643              :  * then some fields may be null'ed out instead of having valid values.
     644              :  *
     645              :  * You should call PQfinish (if conn is not NULL) regardless of whether this
     646              :  * call succeeded.
     647              :  */

    2655              :                                         /*----------
    2656              :                                          * We have three methods of blocking SIGPIPE during
    2657              :                                          * send() calls to this socket:
    2658              :                                          *
    2659              :                                          *      - setsockopt(sock, SO_NOSIGPIPE)
    2660              :                                          *      - send(sock, ..., MSG_NOSIGNAL)
    2661              :                                          *      - setting the signal mask to SIG_IGN during send()
    2662              :                                          *
    2663              :                                          * The third method requires three syscalls per send,
    2664              :                                          * so we prefer either of the first two, but they are
    2665              :                                          * less portable.  The state is tracked in the following
    2666              :                                          * members of PGconn:
    2667              :                                          *
    2668              :                                          * conn->sigpipe_so          - we have set up SO_NOSIGPIPE
    2669              :                                          * conn->sigpipe_flag        - we're specifying MSG_NOSIGNAL
    2670              :                                          *
    2671              :                                          * If we can use SO_NOSIGPIPE, then set sigpipe_so here
    2672              :                                          * and we're done.  Otherwise, set sigpipe_flag so that
    2673              :                                          * we will try MSG_NOSIGNAL on sends.  If we get an error
    2674              :                                          * with MSG_NOSIGNAL, we'll clear that flag and revert to
    2675              :                                          * signal masking.

    4359              : /*
    4360              :  * PQcancel and PQrequestCancel: attempt to request cancellation of the
    4361              :  * current operation.
    4362              :  *
    4363              :  * The return value is true if the cancel request was successfully
    4364              :  * dispatched, false if not (in which case an error message is available).
    4365              :  * Note: successful dispatch is no guarantee that there will be any effect at
    4366              :  * the backend.  The application must read the operation result as usual.
    4367              :  *
    4368              :  * CAUTION: we want this routine to be safely callable from a signal handler
    4369              :  * (for example, an application might want to call it in a SIGINT handler).
    4370              :  * This means we cannot use any C library routine that might be non-reentrant.
    4371              :  * malloc/free are often non-reentrant, and anything that might call them is
    4372              :  * just as dangerous.  We avoid sprintf here for that reason.  Building up
